# PDA Points to Consider No. 12 (2025): Restricted Access Barrier Systems

> 限制進出屏障系統 完整教學版

## Topic 0: Introduction & Glossary 導論與術語 (p1-p7)

# Section 0: Introduction, Glossary & Abbreviations

    

導言、術語表與縮寫

    

PDA Points to Consider No. 12 (2025): Restricted Access Barrier Systems | p1 - p7

    

### 本章學習目標

    

        
- 理解 PDA PtC No. 12 的定位：這是一份專門針對 RABS 的業界最佳實踐指引，而非法規標準

        
- 掌握 RABS 與 Isolator 的根本性差異，以及為何需要獨立的指引文件

        
- 熟悉 RABS 技術中常用的關鍵術語定義，特別是 oRABS / cRABS 的區別

        
- 了解本文件的範圍涵蓋 RABS 全生命週期：設計、確效、操作與屏障系統介面

    

Introduction

    

        

## Original Text

        

This document represents the views of the Parenteral Drug Association (PDA). The document is designed to communicate PDA's thoughts and considerations pertaining to the design, operation, and use of Restricted Access Barrier Systems (RABS) for aseptic processing, processes subjected to terminal sterilization and low bioburden, while encouraging further dialog with industry, health authorities, and suppliers of technologies and materials. This document considers the evolution and needs of the modern, global, sterile, healthcare product manufacturing industry. This document does not represent a standard or regulatory guidance.

        

In 2020, PDA issued Points to Consider for the Aseptic Processing of Sterile Pharmaceutical Products in Isolators, which focus on important regulatory and technology updates surrounding isolator design, validation, and operation for aseptic processing. Several other PDA documents equally address many of the principles for working and operating with RABS, including Points to Consider No. 1: Aseptic Processing (Revised 2023) or Technical Report No. 62 Recommended Practices for Manual Aseptic Processes. Additionally regulatory guidance documents as the European Commission's EU Guidelines for Good Manufacturing Practice for Medicinal Products for Human and Veterinary Use Annex 1: Manufacture of Sterile Medicinal Products (2022), U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) Guidance for Industry: Sterile Drug Products Produced by Aseptic Processing-Current Good Manufacturing Practice (2004) and others are addressing the special requirements for RABS. While many of the recommendations and principles from these documents are equally applicable to RABS, until this point, there was no equivalent guideline or Points to Consider (PtC) dedicated to RABS for which technology and operational specific nuances apply. Hence, a taskforce was established to focus on industry best practices, regulatory and technology considerations directly relevant to the application and use of RABS in an aseptic manufacturing setting.

        

A fundamental principle of sterile product manufacturing is to minimize the risks of contamination (microbiological and particulate) through appropriate facility, equipment, and manufacturing process design, and qualification. The use of barrier systems, including RABS, to increase the protection of the product is not only recommended but should be considered in the context of an overall contamination control and risk-reduction strategy. RABS technology provides for increased product protection compared to non-barrier systems used for Grade A and Grade B aseptic manufacturing operations. RABS is a very different technology to isolators and, consequently, key design, regulatory and operational differences, and considerations apply, most notably background environments, cleaning, disinfection and decontamination methods, aseptic setup, and strictly defined conditions and controls governing open-door RABS interventions.

        

            1 The Pharmaceutical Inspection Co-operation Scheme (PIC/S) Good Manufacturing Practice (GMP) Annex 1 is identical to the European Union (EU) Annex 1 and hereafter EU Annex 1 is also understood to mean EU PIC/S Annex 1.
        

        

As such, this PtC is organized by Topics, followed by relevant points for reader consideration. Each point begins with a problem statement in the form of a question, representing issues or points needing clarification on that specific topic. Recommendations from the authors, who are subject matter experts, are presented in response to each question. The rationale for the recommendation follows, as well as references to support these recommendations, where available. The questions and answers reflect topics suggested by the pharmaceutical industry and recommendations of the members of the task force on what to consider when designing and managing RABS systems with consideration to current regulatory guidance.

    

    

        

## 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 Key Concepts

            

**Restricted Access Barrier Systems, RABS (限制進出屏障系統)：**RABS 是一種用於無菌製程的物理屏障技術。它提供一個封閉但並非完全密封的環境，透過剛性壁面、整合式手套、單向氣流等設計，將操作人員與 Grade A 關鍵區域隔離，從而降低微生物和微粒污染的風險。

            

**PDA (Parenteral Drug Association)：**全球最大的注射劑藥品技術協會，其發布的 Points to Consider 系列文件代表業界專家的共識觀點，雖非法規要求，但在實務中被廣泛採用為最佳實踐依據。

            

**本文件定位：**這是 PDA 首份專門針對 RABS 的完整指引。在此之前，RABS 的相關知識散見於各法規和技術報告中，缺乏系統性的整合。

        

        

            

#### 比喻說明 Analogy

            

想像你在一間高級餐廳的開放式廚房工作。**Isolator (隔離器)** 就像是把整個料理區用密封玻璃罩完全隔離，廚師只能透過手套操作；而 **RABS** 則像是在料理區與用餐區之間設置了透明屏障，廚師主要透過整合的手套操作，但在嚴格控制的條件下可以短暫開門進行特定操作。兩者都比沒有屏障的傳統開放廚房安全得多，但設計邏輯和操作規範截然不同。

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 Key Notes

            

**RABS =/= Isolator：**文件特別強調 RABS 與 Isolator 是「非常不同的技術」(a very different technology)。主要差異包括：

            

                
- **背景環境要求：**RABS 需要 Grade B 背景環境，Isolator 可在 Grade D

                
- **去污方法：**RABS 以手動擦拭消毒為主，Isolator 使用自動化 VPHP 去污

                
- **密封程度：**RABS 不完全密封（有 mouseholes 等開口），Isolator 追求完全隔離

                
- **開門操作：**RABS 在嚴格條件下允許開門介入，Isolator 原則上不開門

            

            

這些差異直接影響設施設計、確效策略和日常操作程序。

        

        

            

#### 法規背景 Regulatory Context

            

本文件頻繁引用的法規基礎：

            

                
- **EU GMP Annex 1 (2022)：**歐盟最新的無菌製造規範，對 RABS 和 Isolator 提出了明確但有區別的要求。PIC/S GMP Annex 1 與之完全相同。

                
- **FDA Guidance (2004)：**美國 FDA 的無菌製程指引，雖然年代較早，但其核心原則仍然適用。

                
- **PDA PtC No. 1 (2023)：**PDA 無菌製程的總體指引，許多原則同樣適用於 RABS。

            

        

        

            

#### 練習思考 Practice Questions

            

                
1. 為什麼 PDA 認為有必要為 RABS 單獨編寫一份 Points to Consider？既有的 Isolator 指引為何不足以涵蓋 RABS？

                
2. 本文件明確聲明「不代表標準或法規指引」，那麼在法規查核（regulatory inspection）時，這份文件扮演什麼角色？

                
3. 如果你的工廠正在評估從傳統開放式充填線升級到 RABS，你會優先關注本文件中的哪些面向？

            

        

    

Scope

    

        

## Original Text

        

This PtC is designed to address key questions and considerations raised from industry relating to the use, application, and operations of RABS in an aseptic manufacturing setting. While the scope of the document relates to considerations of RABS employed for aseptic processing, the principles contained within are equally applicable to RABS for other applications, including products subjected to terminal sterilization and low bioburden processes. In addressing these considerations, the document communicates best practices across the lifecycle of RABS systems including their design and application, qualification, and operation, and extending to barrier system interfaces for both existing and new systems.

    

    

        

## 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 範圍解析 Scope Analysis

            

本文件的範圍涵蓋 RABS 的**全生命週期**：

            

                
- **設計與應用 (Design & Application)：**如何選擇和配置 RABS

                
- **確效 (Qualification)：**如何驗證 RABS 系統符合預期功能

                
- **操作 (Operation)：**日常使用中的最佳實踐

                
- **屏障系統介面 (Barrier System Interfaces)：**RABS 與其他設備的銜接處理

            

            

值得注意的是，雖然主要針對無菌製程 (Aseptic Processing)，但原則也適用於終端滅菌和低生物負荷製程中使用的 RABS。

        

        

            

#### 比喻說明 Analogy

            

這份文件就像是一本**駕駛手冊**：它涵蓋了從買車（設計選擇）、領牌驗車（確效）、日常駕駛（操作）到停車入庫（介面管理）的完整內容。雖然主要是為高速公路駕駛（無菌製程）而寫，但許多規則在一般道路（終端滅菌製程）上也同樣適用。

        

    

Glossary

    

        

## Original Text

        

Definitions have been provided to help clarify the concepts discussed in this document. While some definitions used vary among companies, geographic location, etc., the definitions described below are consistently used within this Points to Consider document. Where a definition is based on another published source, the source is cited.

        
        

Aseptic Process Simulation (APS)

        

A simulation of the entire aseptic manufacturing process in order to verify the capability of the process to assure product sterility. Includes all aseptic operations associated with routine manufacturing, e.g. equipment assembly, formulation, filling, lyophilization and sealing processes as necessary (1).

        
        

Bio-decontamination

        

A process that eliminates bioburden via use of a sporicidal chemical agent (1).

        

*Note: In the context of open RABS (oRABS), this is a manual treatment process with sporicidal agents.*

        
        

Biological Indicator (BI)

        

Test systems that contain viable microorganisms with a defined concentration and resistance to a specific decontamination process. They help monitor whether the necessary conditions were met to kill a specified number of microorganisms for a given process.

        
        

Campaign

        

Processing of multiple lots or batches of the same product serially in the same manufacturing line.

        
        

Contact Time

        

The minimum amount of time that a sanitizer, disinfectant, or sporicide must be left in complete (wet) contact with the surface to be treated in order to be effective (2).

        

*Note: This is typically referred to as "wet contact time".*

        
        

Critical Zone

        

A location within the aseptic processing area in which product and critical surfaces are exposed to the environment (1).

        
        

Critical Surfaces

        

Surfaces that may come directly into contact with, or directly affect, a sterile product or its containers or closures. Critical surfaces are rendered sterile prior to the start of the manufacturing operation, and sterility is maintained throughout processing (1).

        
        

Decontamination

        

The overall process of removal or reduction of any contaminants (chemical, waste, residue, or microorganisms) from an area, object, or person. The method of decontamination used (e.g., cleaning, disinfection, sterilization) should be chosen and validated to achieve a level of cleanliness appropriate to the intended use of the item decontaminated (1). See also Bio-decontamination.

        
        

Disinfection

        

The process by which the reduction of the number of microorganisms is achieved by the irreversible action of a product on their structure or metabolism to a level deemed to be appropriate for a defined purpose (1).

        

*Note: In this document, it is understood that sanitizers and disinfectants are used in the same context.*

        
        

First Air

        

Refers to filtered air that has not been interrupted prior to contacting exposed product and product contact surfaces with the potential to add contamination to the air prior to reaching the critical zone (1).

        
        

Format Parts

        

Container specific parts (e.g., based on different container sizes) that allow the proper guidance/transfer of product containers through a manufacturing line.

        
        

Grade A Air Supply

        

Air which is passed through a filter qualified as capable of producing grade A total particle quality air, but where there is no requirement to perform continuous total particle monitoring or meet grade A viable monitoring limits. Specifically used for the protection of fully stoppered vials where the cap has not yet been crimped (1).

        

*Note: For the purposes of this document, the term Grade A is understood to be interchangeable with International Organization for Standardization (ISO) 5.*

        
        

Hold Time

        

Set durations between qualified events or process steps.

        

Aseptic Hold Time

        

A defined and validated maximum time for 'holding' conditions for aseptic preparation and processing.

        

Clean Hold Time

        

Duration between when cleaning is implemented to meet a target requirement before the use of parts or areas. This type of hold time would typically apply before sterilization or bio-decontamination processes.

        

Sterile Hold Time

        

Duration sterilized items can be held after sterilization and before use.

        
        

Intervention

        

Activities, manipulations, and tasks performed in Grade A, or other critical processing areas, during aseptic operations.

        

Corrective Intervention

        

An intervention that is performed to correct or adjust an aseptic process during its execution. These may not occur at a set frequency in the routine aseptic process. Examples include such activities as clearing component jams, stopping leaks, adjusting sensors, and replacing equipment components.

        

Inherent Intervention

        

An intervention that is an integral part of the aseptic process and is required for either set-up, routine operation and/or monitoring (e.g., aseptic assembly, container replenishment, environmental sampling). Inherent interventions are required by procedure or work instruction for the execution of the aseptic process.

        

Critical Intervention

        

An intervention (corrective or inherent) into the critical zone (1).

        

*Note: An example of this type of intervention would be an open-door intervention when critical surfaces are exposed within the Grade A RABS. This could be a corrective or inherent intervention.*

    

    

        

## 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 - 清潔與去污層級

            

本術語表中有一組容易混淆的概念，需要特別釐清其層級關係：

            

                
- **Cleaning (清潔)：**去除可見污垢與殘留物

                
- **Disinfection (消毒)：**降低微生物數量至適當水平，但不一定能殺滅芽孢

                
- **Bio-decontamination (生物去污)：**使用殺孢子劑消除生物負荷

                
- **Sterilization (滅菌)：**消除所有存活微生物（最高等級）

                
- **Decontamination (去污)：**涵蓋上述所有方法的總稱

            

            

在 RABS 的操作情境中，通常使用 Disinfection 和 Bio-decontamination 而非 Sterilization，因為 RABS 內部表面通常是手動擦拭消毒，而非透過自動化系統進行滅菌。

        

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 - Intervention 介入操作分類

            

Intervention (介入操作) 的分類是 RABS 操作管理中最關鍵的概念之一：

            

                
- **Inherent Intervention (固有介入)：**製程中必須執行的操作，例如環境監測取樣、容器補充。這些是可預期、有計畫的。

                
- **Corrective Intervention (矯正介入)：**因異常而執行的操作，例如清除卡瓶、修復洩漏。這些是不可預期的。

                
- **Critical Intervention (關鍵介入)：**任何進入 Critical Zone 的介入，無論是固有或矯正。在 RABS 環境中，這特別指需要開門的操作。

            

            

RABS 的操作程序設計應盡量減少所有介入操作，尤其是需要開門的 Critical Intervention。

        

        

            

#### 比喻說明 - First Air 初始空氣

            

**First Air (初始空氣)** 的概念可以用淋浴來理解：想像你站在蓮蓬頭下方，水從上方直接流到你身上，這就是「初始水流」；但如果水先碰到牆壁再彈到你身上，那就不再是初始水流了，因為它可能已經攜帶了牆上的髒污。

            

同理，從 HEPA 過濾器出來的空氣直接吹到產品暴露表面，中間沒有被任何障礙物阻擋或擾亂，這就是 First Air。任何阻礙初始空氣的物體都可能在空氣抵達 Critical Zone 之前引入污染。

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 - Hold Time 管理

            

Hold Time（維持時間）在 RABS 操作中扮演關鍵角色。三種 Hold Time 構成了時間控管的完整鏈條：

            

                
- **Clean Hold Time：**清潔完成 → 滅菌/去污開始（確保清潔狀態不劣化）

                
- **Sterile Hold Time：**滅菌完成 → 實際使用（確保無菌狀態維持）

                
- **Aseptic Hold Time：**無菌操作準備完成 → 製程結束（確保無菌製程持續可靠）

            

            

每種 Hold Time 都需要經過驗證 (validation)，超時則需要重新處理。在 RABS 環境中，由於不完全密封的特性，這些時間限制通常比 Isolator 更為嚴格。

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 - Grade A vs ISO 5

            

文件特別註明 **Grade A** 與 **ISO 5** 在本文中可互換使用。但要注意，Grade A 是 EU GMP 的分類（涵蓋微粒和微生物限度），而 ISO 5 是 ISO 14644 的分類（僅涵蓋微粒）。Grade A 在概念上更為嚴格，因為它同時包含微生物監測要求。

            

**Grade A Air Supply** 是一個特殊概念：空氣品質達到 Grade A 微粒標準，但不需要連續微粒監測或符合 Grade A 微生物限度。主要用於完全加塞但尚未鋁蓋封口的小瓶保護。

        

        

            

#### 練習思考 Practice Questions

            

                
1. 在 oRABS 環境中執行 Bio-decontamination 時，為什麼是手動擦拭而非自動化去污？這對操作人員的訓練有什麼影響？

                
2. 試舉出三個在 RABS 充填線上可能發生的 Corrective Intervention 範例，並說明它們為何構成 Critical Intervention。

                
3. 如果 Sterile Hold Time 驗證為 24 小時，但某批次的滅菌零件因排程延遲在 26 小時後才使用，應該如何處理？

            

        

    

Glossary (continued)

    

        

## Original Text

        
        

Isolator

        

A contained, decontaminated environment meeting Grade A/ISO 5 conditions used for aseptic process manufacturing that provides an uncompromised, continuous isolation of its interior from the external environment. Once decontaminated by a validated cycle, an isolator prevents the microbiological contamination of sterile products and product contact surfaces of the interior by enclosures and the supply of continuous, controlled overpressure of HEPA-filtered air (3).

        

Closed Isolator Systems

        

Exclude external contamination from the isolator's interior by accomplishing material transfer via aseptic connection to auxiliary equipment, rather than using openings to the surrounding environment. Closed systems remain sealed throughout operations (1).

        

Open Isolator

        

Systems are designed to allow for the continuous or semi-continuous ingress and/or egress of materials during operations through one or more openings. Openings are engineered (e.g., using continuous overpressure) to exclude the entry of external contamination into the isolator (1).

        
        

Product Contact Parts

        

Direct Product Contact Parts

        

Are those that the product passes through, such as filling needles or pumps (1).

        

Indirect Product Contact Parts

        

Are equipment parts that do not contact the product, but may come into contact with other sterilized surfaces, the sterility of which is critical to the overall product sterility (e.g., sterilized items such as stopper bowls and guides, and sterilized components) (1).

        
        

Rapid Transfer Port (RTP)

        

A System used for the transfer of items into RABS or isolators that minimizes the risk to the critical zone. An example would be a rapid transfer container with an alpha/beta port (1).

        
        

Restricted Access Barrier System (RABS)

        

System that provides an enclosed, but not fully sealed, environment meeting defined air quality conditions (for aseptic processing grade A), and using a rigid-wall enclosure and integrated gloves to separate its interior from the surrounding cleanroom environment. The inner surfaces of the RABS are disinfected and decontaminated with a sporicidal agent. Operators use gloves, half suits, RTPs and other integrated transfer ports to perform manipulations or convey materials to the interior of the RABS. Depending on the design, doors are rarely opened, and only under strictly pre-defined conditions (1).

        

Closed RABS (cRABS)

        

A RABS for which the barrier prevents air exchange with the surrounding environment. Closed RABS uses a dedicated unidirectional air flow unit (UDAF) system for air supply. Unlike a closed isolator, a closed RABS typically has mouseholes, and commonly has no automated biodecontamination system.

        

Open RABS (oRABS)

        

A RABS for which the barrier permits air exchange with the surrounding environment. Passive Open RABS uses the room HVAC for supply. Active Open RABS uses a dedicated unidirectional air flow unit (UDAF) system for air supply but exchanges the exhaust with the room.

        

*Note: Although Open RABS cannot be automatically biodecontaminated, there are some installations where the cleanroom, and all the equipment it contains including the open RABS, is biodecontaminated, but this is a special case.*

        
        

6-Log Reduction

        

The reduction of viable microorganisms with the chance of 1:1,000,000 to have a surviving organism.

        
        

Sporicidal Agent

        

An agent that destroys bacterial and fungal spores when used in sufficient concentration for specified contact time. It is expected to kill all vegetative microorganisms (1).

        
        

Unidirectional Airflow (UDAF)

        

An airflow moving in a single direction, in a robust and uniform manner, and at sufficient speed, to reproducibly sweep particles away from the critical processing or testing area (1).

        

Unidirectional Airflow (UDAF) Unit

        

A cabinet supplied with filtered unidirectional airflow (previously referred to as a Laminar Airflow Unit or LAF) (1).

        
        

Vapor Phase Hydrogen Peroxide (VPHP)

        

Agent for the decontamination of the interior of the isolator, including all exposed surfaces, fixed isolator glove exteriors (portion extending into the barrier), transfer systems, equipment, and certain supplies, materials, and parts, using a defined and validated gaseous mixture or micro-atomization of hydrogen peroxide (H2O2) over a defined and validated period of time, under defined and validated conditions.

        
        

Working Position

        

Position where high-risk operations occur and where product and/or components are exposed (1).

        

*Note: This is sometimes referred to as "working height".*

    

    

        

## 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 - RABS 類型比較

            

RABS 分為兩大類，核心差異在於**空氣系統的隔離程度**：

            
                
                    
                    
                    
                
| 特性 | cRABS (封閉式) | oRABS (開放式) |
| --- | --- | --- |
                
                    
                    
                    
                
| 空氣交換 | 阻止與背景環境的空氣交換 | 允許與背景環境的空氣交換 |
                
                    
                    
                      

                
| 空氣供應 | 專用 UDAF 系統 | 被動式：房間 HVAC主動式：專用 UDAF（排氣至房間） |
                
                    
                    
                    
                
| 自動去污 | 通常無自動化系統（有 mouseholes） | 無法自動去污（特殊案例除外） |
                
                    
                    
                    
                
| 密封程度 | 較高，但仍有 mouseholes | 較低，有意設計的開口 |
            

        

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 - Isolator vs RABS 完整比較

            

將 Isolator 的定義與 RABS 對照，可以清楚看出關鍵差異：

            
                
                    
                    
                    
                
| 特性 | Isolator | RABS |
| --- | --- | --- |
                
                    
                    
                    
                
| 隔離程度 | 完全連續隔離 (uncompromised, continuous isolation) | 封閉但不完全密封 (enclosed, but not fully sealed) |
                
                    
                    
                    
                
| 去污方式 | 經驗證的自動化去污週期（通常 VPHP） | 殺孢子劑消毒（手動擦拭為主） |
                
                    
                    
                    
                
| 正壓維持 | 持續受控正壓 | 視類型而定（cRABS 較能維持） |
                
                    
                    
                    
                
| 物料傳入 | RTP 或密封連接 | 手套、半身衣、RTP |
                
                    
                    
                    
                
| 開門操作 | 原則上不允許 | 在嚴格預定條件下允許 |
            

        

        

            

#### 比喻說明 - cRABS vs oRABS

            

想像兩種不同的手術環境：

            

**cRABS** 就像一間有獨立空調系統的手術室，門通常關著，空氣不會與走廊混合，但門底下仍有小縫隙（mouseholes），需要時可以開門。

            

**oRABS** 就像一間使用走廊空調的手術室，雖然有門和屏障，但空氣會與走廊交換。因此，走廊（Grade B 背景環境）的空氣品質對手術室內的潔淨度至關重要。

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 - 6-Log Reduction

            

**6-Log Reduction (六對數減少)** 是去污效力的重要指標。「6-log」表示微生物數量減少到原來的百萬分之一 (10-6)。

            

在 RABS 環境中，6-log reduction 通常是 bio-decontamination 製程的驗收標準。使用 Biological Indicator (BI) 來驗證去污製程是否達到此標準。

            

對照：Isolator 的 VPHP 去污通常也要求至少 6-log reduction。

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 - RTP 快速傳遞口

            

**Rapid Transfer Port, RTP (快速傳遞口)** 是 RABS 和 Isolator 中用於物料傳入的關鍵裝置。其 alpha/beta port 設計原理：

            

                
- **Alpha port：**安裝在 RABS/Isolator 壁面上的固定部分

                
- **Beta port：**安裝在傳遞容器上的配對部分

                
- 對接時，兩個 port 的外露面（可能受污染的面）被夾在中間，不會接觸到 RABS 內部

            

            

在 RABS 中使用 RTP 可以減少開門操作的需求，是降低污染風險的重要設計。

        

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 - VPHP 與 RABS 的關係

            

注意 **VPHP (汽化過氧化氫)** 的定義中明確提到是用於「isolator 內部的去污」。這反映了一個重要事實：**VPHP 自動去污是 Isolator 的標準配備，但不是 RABS 的標準配備**。

            

RABS（特別是 oRABS）通常依靠手動擦拭殺孢子劑來達成 bio-decontamination。cRABS 雖然結構上更接近 Isolator，但也「通常沒有自動化 biodecontamination 系統」。

            

這個差異對操作程序、人員訓練和確效策略有深遠影響。

        

        

            

#### 實務應用 Practical Application

            

**CDMO 情境：**假設你的 CDMO 工廠目前使用 oRABS 進行無菌充填，一家客戶要求升級到 cRABS。從本術語表的定義出發，你需要考慮的主要變更包括：

            

                
- 空氣供應系統從共用 HVAC 改為專用 UDAF

                
- 屏障設計需要阻止空氣交換（但仍需保留 mouseholes 供容器進出）

                
- 去污程序可能需要重新設計和驗證

                
- Hold Time 參數可能需要重新驗證

                
- 介入操作（Intervention）的程序和評估標準需要更新

            

        

        

            

#### 練習思考 Practice Questions

            

                
1. cRABS 有 mouseholes 但 Closed Isolator 沒有 -- 這個設計差異對污染控制策略有什麼影響？

                
2. 為什麼 Grade A Air Supply 不要求連續微粒監測？在什麼操作階段會使用這種空氣品質等級？

                
3. Direct Product Contact Parts 和 Indirect Product Contact Parts 的滅菌驗證要求有何不同？

                
4. RTP 的 alpha/beta port 設計如何確保傳遞過程中不會引入污染？請畫出或描述對接過程。

            

        

    

Document Structure Overview

    

        

## Original Text

        

As such, this PtC is organized by Topics, followed by relevant points for reader consideration. Each point begins with a problem statement in the form of a question, representing issues or points needing clarification on that specific topic. Recommendations from the authors, who are subject matter experts, are presented in response to each question. The rationale for the recommendation follows, as well as references to support these recommendations, where available.

    

    

        

## 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 文件結構解析

            

本 PtC 採用的 Q&A 結構非常有特色，每個議題包含四個層次：

            

                
1. **Problem Statement (問題陳述)：**以提問形式呈現業界實際面臨的疑問

                
2. **Recommendation (建議)：**由專家小組提出的最佳實踐建議

                
3. **Rationale (理據)：**解釋為什麼如此建議

                
4. **References (參考文獻)：**支持建議的文獻依據

            

            

這種結構使得讀者可以直接找到與自身問題相關的議題，而不必通讀全文。在後續章節的學習中，請注意識別這四個層次。

        

    

    

### 本節重點回顧 Section Summary

    

        
- **文件定位：**PDA PtC No. 12 是首份專門針對 RABS 的業界指引，代表專家共識而非法規要求，但在實務中具有重要參考價值

        
- **RABS vs Isolator：**兩者是根本不同的技術，在密封程度、去污方式、背景環境要求和開門操作規範上有本質差異

        
- **RABS 兩大類型：**cRABS（封閉式）阻止空氣交換並使用專用 UDAF；oRABS（開放式）允許空氣交換，對背景環境要求更高

        
- **關鍵術語：**掌握 Critical Zone、First Air、Intervention 分類、Hold Time 類型、Bio-decontamination 等核心概念，是理解後續章節的基礎

        
- **全生命週期範圍：**本文件涵蓋 RABS 的設計、確效、操作和介面管理，適用於無菌製程及終端滅菌/低生物負荷製程

        
- **Q&A 結構：**後續章節採用 Problem Statement → Recommendation → Rationale → References 的四層結構

## Topic 1: RABS Design RABS設計 (p8-p33)

# Section 1a: Topic 1 — Restricted Access Barrier System Design (Q1.1–Q1.6)

    

主題 1（上）：限制進出屏障系統設計

    

PDA Points to Consider No. 12 (2025) | p8 – p17

    

### 本章學習目標

- 掌握 RABS 設計準則屬性（屏障、氣流、手套口、RTP、環境控制、壓差、清潔與生物去污）的關鍵比較

        
- 瞭解 cRABS 相較於 oRABS 與 Isolator 的獨特設計考量

        
- 認識 RABS 手套口定位、手套材質選擇與操作介入管控的設計原則

        
- 理解如何透過設計降低人員介入對無菌保證的風險

    

    

### 本節快速導覽

    

        Q1.1 RABS 類型
        Q1.2 設計準則
        Q1.3 cRABS 設計

        Q1.5 RABS 手套設計

Q 1.1 What are the different types of restricted access barrier systems (RABS)?

    

        

### 原文內容 Original Text

        

**Recommendation**

        

A Restricted Access Barrier System (RABS) is a series of components and processes that enclose and provide a Grade A environment for aseptic processing (e.g., dispensing, filling and closing, lyophilization loading). Due to the protection offered by the barrier system, a RABS can provide a higher level of product and personnel protection than conventional Grade A or Grade B filling operations. See Question 2.3.

        

All RABS have rigid barriers, glove ports for operator access, a unidirectional airflow (UDAF) unit source providing H14 high efficiency particulate air filter (HEPA) filtered air (i.e., First Air), and a method to transfer materials and supplies in and out of it. Having these features in common, RABS differentiate in three different types of air handling: passive open RABS (oRABS), active oRABS, and closed RABS (cRABS), each offering an increasing level of protection for product and personnel. See Topic 3.

        

*Note: This document does not cover isolator design. (See PDA’s Point to Consider for the Aseptic Processing of Sterile Pharmaceuticals in Isolators for additional information.)*

        

Figures 1.1-1, 1.1-2, and 1.1-3 depict the general layout of each RABS type highlighting the UDAF source, rigid barrier coverage, and typical environmental classifications.

        

*Note: Diagrams are provided to illustrate the ways that air is supplied to and exits from the different types of RABS systems. Diagrams are not intended to inform readers how operators should interact with the equipment enclosed; that detail follows in later sections.*

        

**Figure 1.1-1:** Passive oRABS  

        **Figure 1.1-2:** Active oRABS  

        **Figure 1.1-3:** cRABS

        

**Rationale**

        

Product and aseptic procedures could require different designs of RABS systems. The correct execution of the RABS needs to be evaluated during the design process of the filling line and should be made based on a risk assessment.

    

    

        

### 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 Key Concepts

            

**RABS (限制進出屏障系統)：**RABS 是一套由硬質屏障、手套口、HEPA 過濾單向氣流、物料傳遞口等元件組成的系統，目的是在無菌製程區域形成 Grade A 環境，將操作人員與關鍵區域「隔離」，降低微生物污染風險。

            

**三種 RABS 類型的核心差異在於氣流處理方式：**

            

                
- **Passive oRABS（被動開放式）：**氣流來自房間天花板 HVAC 系統，經屏障後溢流至周圍空間。保護等級最低。

                
- **Active oRABS（主動開放式）：**配備專屬 RABS HVAC 系統供氣，但氣流仍溢流至周圍空間。保護等級中等。

                
- **cRABS（封閉式）：**配備專屬 HVAC 系統，氣流在 RABS 內部循環不外溢，可建立正壓差。保護等級最高。

            

            

**First Air (第一氣流)：**指從 HEPA 過濾器出來後尚未接觸任何表面的潔淨氣流，是保護無菌產品的第一道防線。

        

        

            

#### 比喻說明 Analogy

            

想像一間手術室：

            

                
- **Passive oRABS** 就像手術室只靠走廊的空調吹氣，門是半開的 — 有基本保護但容易受走廊環境影響。

                
- **Active oRABS** 像手術室有自己的獨立空調，但門仍半開 — 空氣品質更好，但走廊的人走過還是有影響。

                
- **cRABS** 像手術室有獨立空調且門關上 — 內部空氣循環使用，與外界隔離，提供最高保護。

            

            

而 Isolator（隔離器）則像太空站 — 完全密封、自成一體，本文件不涵蓋此範圍。

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 Key Notes

            

**保護等級遞增順序：**Passive oRABS < Active oRABS < cRABS < Isolator。選擇哪種類型應基於風險評估 (Risk Assessment)，考量產品特性、製程需求、人員安全等因素。

            

PDA 明確指出，「Non-barrier technology（無屏障技術）」已是過時技術，不符合法規期望。所有新建線體應至少採用 RABS。

        

        

            

#### 練習思考 Practice Questions

            

                
1. 請說明 Passive oRABS 與 Active oRABS 在氣流來源上的根本差異是什麼？

                
2. 若您的產品具有毒性，三種 RABS 中哪一種可以使用？為什麼？

                
3. 為什麼 PDA 說「Non-barrier technology 已過時」？從法規趨勢（如 EU GMP Annex 1, 2022）的角度說明。

            

        

    

Q 1.2 What are the design criteria considerations for restricted access barrier systems (RABS)?

    

        

### 原文內容 Original Text

        

**Recommendation**

        

There are several design criteria attributes that need to be taken into consideration when selecting the type of RABS appropriate for a filling line (1, 5, 6).

        

Table 1.2-1 summarizes the main design criteria attributes that need to be taken into consideration for each type of RABS.

        

**Table 1.2-1: RABS and Non-Barrier System Design Criteria Attribute Considerations**

        

        
            
                
                
                
                
                
            
| Design Attribute | Non-Barrier System* | Passive Open RABS | Active Open RABS | Closed RABS |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
            
                ****
                
                
                
                
            
| Barrier | No barrier system; Open to the room; Leak Rate Test unable to be performed | Barrier system; Open to the room; Leak Rate Test unable to be performed | Barrier system; Open to the room; Leak Rate Test unable to be performed | Barrier system; Closed to the room; Leak Rate Test able to be performed |
            
                ****
                
                
                
                
            
| Unidirectional Airflow Source | HVAC system mounted in surrounding space/room | HVAC system mounted in surrounding space/room | Dedicated RABS HVAC system | Dedicated RABS HVAC system |
            
                ****
                
                
                
                
            
| Glove Ports | None | Glove ports installed on rigid barrier | Glove ports installed on rigid barrier | Glove ports installed on rigid barrier |
            
                ****
                
                
                
                
            
| Rapid Transfer Ports (RTPs) | None | Material transfer ports integrated into rigid barrier | Material transfer ports integrated into rigid barrier | Material transfer ports integrated into rigid barrier |
            
                ****
                
                
                
                
            
| Environmental Control | Factors controlled by HVAC in surrounding space/room; No pressure differential | Factors controlled by HVAC in surrounding space/room; Minimal to no pressure differential | Factors controlled by dedicated RABS HVAC system; Pressure differential | Factors controlled by dedicated RABS HVAC system; Pressure differential |
            
                ****
                
                
                
                
            
| Pressure Cascade | No pressure cascade possible | No pressure cascade possible | No pressure cascade possible | Pressure cascade possible |
            
                ****
                
                
                
                
            
| Cleaning | Manual | Manual | Manual | Manual or possible installation of automatic system with spray balls (Wetting/Washing In Place) and/or semiautomatic system with spray guns |
            
                ****
                
                
                
                
            
| Bio-decontamination | Possible only with room | Possible only with room | Possible only with room | Possible w/o room, but the absence of an inflatable gasket could generate leakage and should not be performed without appropriate precautions for personnel safety |
            
                ****
                
                
                
                
            
| Product | Nontoxic | Nontoxic | Nontoxic | Nontoxic & Toxic |
        

        

        

** "Non-barrier technology" is obsolete technology.*  

        *Note: Biosafety Cabinets (BSCs) are not covered under the scope of this table.*

        

**Barrier Considerations**

        

Non-barrier technology is obsolete and is not compliant with regulatory expectations. Non-barrier systems have only individual barriers in place, such as polycarbonate, or curtains and aseptic operations are open to the surrounding space of the room.

        

All types of RABS have a barrier system in place (e.g., translucent rigid barriers) that surrounds the aseptic operations. In oRABS (i.e., passive and active), the barrier system is open to the room via openings below the product level that allow the unidirectional airflow to vent to the surrounding space. This type of oRABS is not sufficiently sealed during operations, therefore the RABS cannot be subjected to a Leak Rate Test to verify enclosure integrity while in operation.

        

In cRABS, the barrier system is closed to the room such that the unidirectional airflow is recirculated inside the cRABS. The barrier system is sealed, and the cRABS may be subjected to a Leak Rate Test to verify closure integrity even during operations. However, the lack of inflatable gaskets can lead to leaking into the room, and the Leak Rate Test should not be conducted without additional precautionary measures.

        

**Unidirectional Airflow Source**

        

Non-barrier systems and passive oRABS have unidirectional airflow supplied by the surrounding space/room via a ceiling-mounted HVAC system with HEPA-grade filters. Active oRABS and cRABS have unidirectional airflow supplied by a dedicated RABS HVAC system with HEPA-grade filters.

        

**Glove Ports**

        

Non-barrier systems do not have glove ports because the process is open to the surrounding space/room. All types of RABS have glove port(s) installed on the rigid barrier; number and placement will vary. Glove ports allow for aseptic interventions to occur without the need for the operator to enter the RABS (i.e., aseptic processing area).

        

**Rapid Transfer Ports (RTPs)**

        

Non-barrier systems have no material transfer ports because supplies and samples that are transferred into and out of the processing area are done so directly. (See Topic 6 for additional information.) All types of RABS have material transfer port(s) that are integrated into RABS. These ports allow for the aseptic transfer of materials and samples in and out of the RABS.

        

*Note: Although RABS doors can be opened, in the absence of appropriate controls this would potentially allow the introduction of lower-grade air into the Grade A space, potentially contaminating the Grade A processing area environment with lower-grade air. Open-door interventions should be extremely rare occurrences, and proper risk mitigation precautions should be implemented (1).*

        

**Environmental Control**

        

Factors such as temperature, humidity, and differential pressure are controlled by the HVAC unit mounted in the surrounding room/space for non-barrier systems and passive oRABS. These factors are controlled by the dedicated RABS HVAC unit for active oRABS and cRABS.

        

Typically, no positive pressure is present over the processing area compared to the surrounding space. Minimal to no positive pressure is present in passive oRABS over the processing area compared to the surrounding space. In active oRABS and cRABS, positive pressure is established in the processing area compared to the surrounding space. However, in some designs there is the capability to selectively control the air volume in specific areas to enable a positive air flow.

        

**Pressure Cascade**

        

No pressure cascade is possible in non-barrier systems, or oRABS (i.e., active or passive), but this is possible in cRABS.

        

**Bio-decontamination**

        

Bio-decontamination (by gassing or fogging) is possible for non-barrier systems or oRABS only if the room is also bio-decontaminated. In the case of cRABS, it is possible to perform bio-decontamination without the room, however, if the cRABS does not utilize inflatable gaskets, there could be leakage around the gaskets leading to health safety concerns and adequate precautions are needed to ensure personnel safety.

        

**Product**

        

Only nontoxic products are able to be manufactured in non-barrier systems and in oRABS (i.e., active or passive). In cRABS, it is possible to manufacture nontoxic or toxic drug products.

        

**Additional design features** should be considered including, but not limited to the following:

        

            
- Design must ensure that all processes (i.e., with the exception of setup) will be designed to avoid open-door interventions.

            
- The barrier walls should be rigid, resistant to chemical cleaning and disinfecting agents, and also resistant to mechanical stresses (e.g., scratches/cracking) from cleaning tools. Typical barrier materials are polycarbonate or tempered/safety glass.

            
- The positioning of equipment, components, and sensors within the critical zone (e.g., filling needles, open vials) should be considered to ensure that First Air is not disrupted. For fixed machine components (i.e., transport mechanisms), having an effective disinfection program in place is required.

            
- The glove positions inside the RABS barrier wall should be appropriate to allow operator arm entry into RABS glove(s) without disruption of First Air above critical surfaces, for example, open vials at the accumulation turntable, above fill needles, above stopper bowl, or above environmental monitoring (EM) equipment. It is key that these locations be determined early in the design process and tested during the mock-up phase of the project to verify operator ergonomics for all intended operations. Having support from experienced operators during this design process is beneficial and recommended.

        

        

*Note: Any tools that are stored inside the RABS for operator use must be sterilized.*

        

            
- To protect the product from particulate contamination, it is recommended that RABS parts and components in the aseptic processing area be constructed of non-shedding, non-leaching, non-corrosive, chemical-resistant materials. It is recommended that all metallic components be constructed of low-carbon 304 stainless steel or better. In the case of metallic product contact and indirect product-contact components, low-carbon 316 stainless steel or better should be used (5). All nonmetallic materials, including RABS gloves, gasketing, seals, and barrier walls and doors need to withstand exposure to various cleaning and disinfecting agents and be suitable for the process.

        

        

The following are some points to consider in design and operations of RABS that impact achieving specified environmental control conditions within the RABS:

        

            
- Appropriate lighting to see the equipment, product, and components without degradation of light sensitive product.

            
- Rounded corners and smooth materials to minimize the risk of compromising the glove integrity during changes or line interventions.

            
- Safety curtain (i.e., light curtain) to detect operator glove entry into the RABS.

            
- Alarms for environmental parameters (Temperature/Humidity/UDAF velocity) and door status (door open or closed).

            
- EM system viable and total particles in continuous operation during setup and filling operations.

            
- EM system (settle plates and active air-monitoring locations) readily accessible via glove ports.

        

        

**Rationale**

        

The RABS design attributes as described in Table 1.2-1 are beneficial in assuring that environmental conditions are maintained and minimizing microbial contamination associated with direct human interventions in the critical zones.

    

    

        

### 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 Key Concepts

            

**Table 1.2-1 是本節的核心。**這張比較表從 9 個設計屬性維度，系統性地比較了四種技術（含已過時的 Non-Barrier）。以下是最關鍵的幾個區別：

            

                
- **Leak Rate Test (洩漏率測試)：**只有 cRABS 因為密封到房間，才能執行此測試來驗證屏障完整性。oRABS 因為底部有開口溢氣，無法執行。

                
- **Pressure Cascade (壓力梯度)：**只有 cRABS 可以建立壓力梯度 — 這對於控制氣流方向、防止低潔淨等級的空氣倒灌至關重要。

                
- **Bio-decontamination (生物去污)：**oRABS 只有連同房間一起去污才可行；cRABS 可獨立去污（但需注意密封墊片的洩漏問題）。

                
- **毒性產品：**只有 cRABS 可處理毒性藥品，因其密封特性可同時保護產品與操作人員。

            

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 Key Notes

            

**材質規範：**

            

                
- 一般金屬部件：低碳 304 不鏽鋼或更高等級

                
- 產品接觸及間接接觸部件：低碳 316 不鏽鋼或更高等級

                
- 非金屬材料（手套、墊片、密封件、屏障壁與門）：須耐受各種清潔與消毒劑

                
- 屏障壁材料：聚碳酸酯 (Polycarbonate) 或鋼化/安全玻璃

            

            

**設計原則：**所有製程（設置/setup 除外）都必須設計為避免開門介入 (Open-door Interventions)。存放在 RABS 內的工具必須經過滅菌。

        

        

            

#### 比喻說明 Analogy

            

這張比較表就像選擇汽車的安全等級：

            

                
- **Non-Barrier** = 沒有安全帶的老車（已被法規淘汰）

                
- **Passive oRABS** = 有安全帶但沒有安全氣囊的車

                
- **Active oRABS** = 有安全帶加安全氣囊的車

                
- **cRABS** = 全車主動安全系統（ABS + 氣囊 + 車道偏離警示 + 自動煞車）

            

            

安全等級越高，成本越高，但保護也越全面。選擇依據是風險評估。

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 — 環境監測設計

            

PDA 列出的環境控制設計考量極為實務：

            

                
- **Light Curtain（光柵）：**偵測操作員手套進入 RABS 的自動感應系統 — 可用於記錄介入事件

                
- **環境參數警報：**溫度/濕度/UDAF 風速/門開關狀態 — 任何偏離都需要即時告警

                
- **EM 系統：**沉降板與主動空氣採樣位置必須能透過手套口操作 — 這直接影響手套口的定位設計

                
- **圓角與光滑材料：**減少手套在操作中被尖銳邊角損壞的風險

            

        

        

            

#### 實務應用 Practical Application

            

**CDMO 場景：**假設您的 CDMO 正在評估一條新建充填線的屏障技術選型。客戶 A 需要充填抗體藥物（非毒性），客戶 B 需要充填 ADC 藥物（毒性原料藥）。

            

                
- 客戶 A 的產品：oRABS 或 cRABS 皆可，視整體 CCS 與風險評估決定

                
- 客戶 B 的產品：**必須使用 cRABS**（或 Isolator），因為只有封閉系統才能同時保護產品無菌性與操作人員安全

                
- 若要最大化線體利用率，採用 cRABS 可兼顧兩類客戶需求

            

        

        

            

#### 練習思考 Practice Questions

            

                
1. 為什麼 oRABS 無法進行 Leak Rate Test？從其氣流設計的角度解釋。

                
2. cRABS 在沒有 Inflatable Gasket（充氣密封墊）的情況下進行生物去污，會有什麼安全風險？

                
3. PDA 建議產品接觸部件使用 316 不鏽鋼而非 304 不鏽鋼，原因是什麼？（提示：考慮耐腐蝕性與產品相容性）

                
4. 為什麼手套口定位要在設計早期（mock-up 階段）就由有經驗的操作員參與確認？

            

        

    

Q 1.3 What are the design criteria for closed restricted access barrier systems (cRABS)?

    

        

### 原文內容 Original Text

        

**Recommendation**

        

A cRABS, while not providing the same design constructs as an isolator, does provide some advantages over an oRABS design. The benefits of a cRABS can only be experienced when the RABS remains closed following setup. All qualified interventions should be able to be performed through the glove ports. The need to open the doors should be rare and heavily scrutinized on a case-by-case basis; these types of rare open-door interventions may require a deviation (1, 3, 6).

        

**Differences between cRABS and active oRABS:**

        

            
- The rigid barrier completely encloses the Grade A space within the cRABS.

            
- Air is recirculated within a cRABS, hence there is no spillover to adjacent space as in an oRABS. (See Figure 1.1-3.)

            
- Pressure can be maintained within a cRABS, allowing for better control of a pressure cascade between the RABS and upstream and downstream equipment.

        

        

**Differences between cRABS and an isolator:**

        

            
- If inflatable door seals on a cRABS are not present, a vapor-phase hydrogen peroxide (VPHP) cycle is not recommended without adequate safety precautions.

            
- Due to the lack of a positive door seal, the background environment for a cRABS is Grade B to minimize the risk of contamination.

            
- In the case of rare, open-door interventions and the potential for not being able to conduct automated biodecontamination for a cRABS, a Grade B background is required to minimize the risk of contamination.

        

        

**Rationale**

        

The cRABS design attributes are beneficial in providing further assurance of environmental conditions and minimizing microbial contamination associated with direct human interventions in the critical zones.

    

    

        

### 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 Key Concepts

            

**cRABS 的定位 — 介於 oRABS 與 Isolator 之間：**

            

                
- 相較 oRABS：cRABS 的屏障完全封閉 Grade A 空間、氣流內部循環、可建立壓力梯度

                
- 相較 Isolator：cRABS 缺乏正壓門封 (Positive Door Seal)，因此背景環境須為 Grade B（Isolator 背景可為 Grade C 或 D）

            

            

**VPHP (汽化過氧化氫)：**一種常用的表面生物去污方法。由於 cRABS 若無充氣密封墊片 (Inflatable Gasket)，VPHP 可能洩漏到周圍環境，對人員造成安全風險，因此須格外謹慎。

        

        

            

#### 比喻說明 Analogy

            

如果將 Isolator 想成一間完全密封的「太空站」，那 cRABS 就像一間「高級潛水艇」— 雖然有密封門艙，但門封不像太空站那麼嚴密。因此：

            

                
- 太空站（Isolator）可以在太空（Grade C/D 背景）安全運作

                
- 潛水艇（cRABS）需要在較淺的水域（Grade B 背景）運作，才能在門封不完美時維持安全

            

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 Key Notes

            

**cRABS 最關鍵的操作原則：**Setup 完成後，門必須保持關閉，直到批次結束。所有合格介入 (Qualified Interventions) 都應能透過手套口完成。若必須開門，應視為極罕見事件，逐案審查，且可能需要開立偏差 (Deviation)。

            

這個原則直接影響到：

            

                
- 手套口的數量與位置必須足以涵蓋所有預期操作

                
- 設備設計必須讓所有維護操作都能從手套口完成

                
- 人員訓練必須確保熟練使用手套口作業

            

        

        

            

#### 練習思考 Practice Questions

            

                
1. 為什麼 cRABS 的背景環境必須是 Grade B 而非 Grade C？從門封設計的角度解釋。

                
2. 如果 cRABS 配備了充氣密封墊片 (Inflatable Gasket)，這會改變哪些設計考量？

            

        

    

Q 1.4 What are the design considerations for the placement of the restricted access barrier system (RABS) glove ports?

    

        

### 原文內容 Original Text

        

**Recommendation**

        

The correct positioning of the RABS glove ports is one of the key elements that should be considered during the design of a RABS. The position of the glove ports plays a vital role in the operation of the RABS and its ability to remain closed during setup and operation. Efforts to minimize the need to use RABS gloves should be taken to reduce the impact or risk to process performance and product sterility. Examples include reducing, eliminating, or repositioning activities, manipulations, and interventions. Figure 1.4-1 distinguishes which part of the RABS are the glove ports and which are the RABS gloves (1).

        

*Figure 1.4-1: Differentiation of Glove Ports and Gloves*

        

When determining where to place/position the RABS glove ports (typically done during mock-up studies), several factors that may pose a risk to the performance of the aseptic process and sterility of the product should be considered such as:

        

            
- Use of a simulation method to review glove port positioning

            
- Ergonomics to address personnel fatigue and safety

            
- Diversity of personnel height and reach, from which a determined range may inform optimum port positioning

            
- Quantity of glove ports

            
- Orientation and location of planned and anticipated activities, manipulations, and interventions (i.e., inherent and corrective interventions)

            
- Glove port distance to open containers (e.g., vials, syringes, cartridges, EM components) and equipment*

            
- RABS gloves range of motion

            
- Weight and orientation of materials and items to be handled via the glove port

            
- Ability to install RABS gloves and donning RABS gloves in an aseptic manner

            
- Orientation of RABS gloves during decontamination/disinfection, aeration, if applicable, and nonuse

            
- Proximity to sharp objects or surfaces that can pierce RABS gloves

            
- Position of EM apparatus, instruments, and sampling sites

        

        

**Note: Interventions cannot be performed directly using the RABS gloves, but rather by using a sterilized tool and/or sterile material for an additional layer of protection where the First Air concept needs to be maintained.*

        

**Rationale**

        

With the use of RABS gloves, it is possible to perform interventions inside the RABS without the need to open it. The correct positioning of glove ports enables the operator to reach machine parts without the introduction of the operator gloves and gown, which are potential particle and microbial contamination sources. For this reason, the design and position of glove ports is an important decision point and should be part of the risk assessment and contamination control strategy (CCS).

        

Generally, a review of the positioning should be performed using a simulation method. Modeling, rendering, 3-D model, virtual reality, mock-up, or any method that allows for demonstration and testing of glove-related procedures with different operators of diverse heights and arm length could be used.

        

The glove port needs to be positioned to ensure that the RABS gloves have sufficient distance to the open containers (e.g., vials, syringes, cartridges, EM components, etc.) and to the equipment that comes into direct and indirect contact with the product. This allows for a RABS glove entry by the operator without disruption for First Air above critical surfaces.

        

The design of glove ports should be sufficiently cleanable (i.e., hygienic design) and resistant to the appropriate cleaning/disinfection agents. The design should also allow for the range of motion necessary with the RABS gloves to avoid excessive operator reaching or stretching of RABS gloves.

        

Restriction of airflow interrupting or interfering with adequate distribution of decontamination chemicals, vapors, or gases (i.e., typically only seen with cRABS) should be avoided.

        

If applicable, select position of glove stretchers to allow for automatic bio-decontamination of the whole surface (cRABS only).

    

    

        

### 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 Key Concepts

            

**Glove Port（手套口）vs. Gloves（手套）：**這是兩個不同的元件。Glove Port 是安裝在屏障壁上的固定開口與法蘭結構；Gloves 是安裝在 Port 上的可更換手套。兩者的設計考量不同：

            

                
- **Port 定位：**決定操作員能觸及的範圍 — 一旦屏障壁製造完成就難以更改

                
- **Gloves 選擇：**材質、厚度、尺寸 — 可更換但須匹配 Port 設計

            

            

**Mock-up Studies（模型試驗）：**PDA 強調手套口定位必須在設計早期透過模擬或實體模型進行驗證。方法包括 3D 模型、虛擬實境 (VR)、實體 Mock-up 等，且須讓不同身高與臂長的操作員參與測試。

        

        

            

#### 比喻說明 Analogy

            

手套口的設計就像設計汽車駕駛座：

            

                
- 方向盤、排檔桿、按鈕的位置必須讓不同身材的駕駛都能舒適操作

                
- 如果設計不當，高個子碰不到腳踏板，矮個子看不到儀表板

                
- 駕駛座一旦出廠就無法大幅更改 — 手套口也是如此

            

            

因此，在「交車前」（設備出廠前）就要讓各種身材的「試駕員」（操作員）來驗證。

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 Key Notes

            

**關鍵設計原則 — 間距：**手套口與開放容器（開口瓶、注射器等）之間必須有足夠距離，確保操作員手臂進入 RABS 手套時不會干擾 First Air。這是一個經常在設計審查中被忽略但在實際運行中引發問題的關鍵點。

            

**注意：**PDA 明確指出，操作員不應直接使用 RABS 手套觸碰產品或關鍵表面，而應使用已滅菌的工具或無菌材料作為額外保護層。這是一個常見的操作誤解。

        

        

            

#### 練習思考 Practice Questions

            

                
1. 列舉三種可用來驗證手套口定位的模擬方法，並比較其優缺點。

                
2. 為什麼 PDA 建議手套口位置需考慮「接近尖銳物體的距離」？這與哪些風險有關？

                
3. 在 cRABS 中，手套伸展器 (Glove Stretcher) 的位置為什麼會影響生物去污效果？

            

        

    

Q 1.5 What are the design considerations for restricted access barrier system (RABS) gloves?

    

        

### 原文內容 Original Text

        

**Recommendation**

        

Quality risk management (QRM) principles should be used to identify, assess, and address special considerations for the safe and effective use of RABS gloves to mitigate the risks posed by the installation and use of RABS gloves during aseptic operation (1).

        

Once the glove-port positioning is determined, a number of factors that may pose a risk to the performance of the aseptic process and the sterility of the product should be considered. The following considerations should be given to the composition of RABS gloves (3, 4):

        

            
- Quality and design of RABS gloves should be sufficiently cleanable (i.e., hygienic design) and resistant to the appropriate cleaning/disinfection agents and steam sterilization.

            
- Glove size, though usually supplied as standard size ranges, should be considered based on intended user population and demographic to ensure that gloves are sufficiently sized and practical for use.

            
- Method of physical and visual inspection for integrity (See Topic 4).

            
- Ability to confirm or test the integrity of RABS gloves (See Topic 4).

            
- Ability to decontaminate, disinfect and, if applicable, aerate RABS gloves

            
- Selection of glove material (e.g., ethylene propylene diene monomer (EPDM), chlorosulfonated polyethylene synthetic rubber (CSM)) to allow for resistance during sanitization/decontamination and use; also, to ensure sufficient dexterity to allow for the accurate execution of interventions

            
- Thickness of glove material to address dexterity needed to perform task in RABS gloves

            
- Thickness of glove material to resist puncture, cracking, or excessive wear

            
- Ability to adequately install RABS gloves in glove ports to maintain aseptic status of the line

        

        

Additional operational considerations include, but are not limited to:

        

            
- A sufficient number of spare RABS gloves should be available for each run.

            
- Expiration date of RABS gloves

            
- Exposure to direct sunlight that can degrade RABS gloves or glove seal material

            
- Safe position for intermediate storage of RABS gloves in the RABS glove port after or between operations to avoid both the obstruction to First Air during operation, as well as ensuring that the gloves cannot be damaged by moving parts within the RABS

        

        

**Rationale**

        

Performing the above recommendations will reduce the possibility of leakages due to the tearing of RABS gloves, which impacts the integrity of the RABS. These recommendations are to promote compliance of good aseptic practices/techniques to reduce contamination risks and promote the prevention of open-door interventions.

        

With the use of RABS gloves, it is possible to perform interventions inside the RABS and to reach machine parts without the introduction of the operator gloves and gown (a potential particle and microbial contamination source). For this reason, the manner of usage, construction materials, and installation procedures is an important decision point and should, at a minimum, be recorded in the CCS.

    

    

        

### 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 Key Concepts

            

**RABS 手套材質選擇是一個典型的工程折衷 (Trade-off)：**

            

                
- **EPDM（三元乙丙橡膠）：**耐蒸氣滅菌、耐化學藥品、彈性佳，是常見選擇

                
- **CSM（氯磺化聚乙烯合成橡膠）：**化學抗性好、耐臭氧與紫外線

                
- **厚度的取捨：**太薄 → 容易穿刺破損；太厚 → 靈巧度不足，操作員疲勞

            

            

**手套完整性測試 (Glove Integrity Testing)：**PDA 將此獨立為 Topic 4 討論，強調了其重要性。手套破損意味著 RABS 屏障完整性被破壞，相當於「城牆出現缺口」。

        

        

            

#### 比喻說明 Analogy

            

RABS 手套的設計就像外科手術手套的進階版：

            

                
- 外科手套要兼顧觸感（薄）與防護（不破）— RABS 手套也是

                
- 外科手套有尺碼選擇 — RABS 手套也需要考慮使用者群體的手型

                
- 但 RABS 手套還要能耐受蒸氣滅菌、化學消毒劑、VPHP 等嚴苛條件 — 遠超外科手套的要求

            

            

而且外科手套用完即丟，RABS 手套則是可重複使用，因此還有有效期限、儲存條件、紫外線降解等額外考量。

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 Key Notes

            

**操作面的實務考量常被設計者忽略：**

            

                
- **備品管理：**每次運行必須備有足夠的備用手套 — 若手套在批次中破損且無備品，可能需要開門更換（最壞情況）

                
- **非使用時的手套位置：**手套不能懸垂在 First Air 路徑上阻擋氣流，也不能被 RABS 內的運動部件損壞

                
- **陽光曝曬：**直射陽光會加速橡膠降解 — 這在有天窗或大面積玻璃窗的潔淨室中是實際問題

            

            

PDA 強調手套的使用方式、構造材料與安裝程序至少應記錄在 CCS (污染控制策略) 中。

        

        

            

#### 練習思考 Practice Questions

            

                
1. EPDM 與 CSM 兩種手套材質各適用於什麼場景？如果您的 cRABS 需要使用 VPHP 生物去污，會傾向選擇哪種材質？

                
2. 手套厚度如何影響操作員的介入品質？在「精細操作」與「耐久性」之間如何取得平衡？

                
3. 為什麼 PDA 要求手套相關資訊必須記錄在 CCS 中？

            

        

    

Q 1.6 How should the restricted access barrier system (RABS) be designed to minimize the risk posed by interventions?

    

        

### 原文內容 Original Text

        

**Recommendation**

        

Human interventions (i.e., open-door and/or inherent interventions) within the RABS are required during the setup and assembly of the aseptic filling machine, including the installation of RABS gloves, and during routine manufacturing operations (e.g., aseptic filling with open- and closed-door inherent and corrective interventions).

        

Risk-based assessments should be used to evaluate the need for and design of human interventions. Where possible, interventions should be eliminated, reduced, or modified to reduce their relative risk. A process should be created to monitor and control the frequency of interventions. Changes to the process should be made to improve the overall robustness of the manufacturing process and should eliminate the need for interventions, when possible.

        

It is not recommended to approach the need for manufacturing changes with the goal of reducing intervention. Corrective, open-door interventions should be eliminated or occur only as very rare events. Therefore, the prevention of open-door interventions should be a key factor in the consideration for designing a RABS (1, 6).

        

The positioning of RABS gloves in proper locations should eliminate the need for open-door interventions during filling operations where good aseptic technique applies. Interventions within the RABS (i.e., inherent and corrective) are to be designed to minimize microbiological ingress, including retention, within the RABS. Such factors are proximity to exposed sterile product, components, indirect product contact surfaces, intervention duration, complexity, and frequency.

        

The following points for consideration are applicable for an aseptic filling line and also for other aseptic working steps (e.g., dispensing, lyophilizer loading/unloading), where a RABS is used:

        

            
- The RABS and the filling line should be designed to allow for interventions (i.e., open and closed door) in the Grade A RABS with due consideration of adherence to proper aseptic technique, for example, to follow First Air working principles for the operator during open-door interventions and also RABS gloves during closed-door interventions. See Question 1.1 for more information.

            
- In the case of an open-door intervention that requires direct entry of part of the operator’s body within the Grade A area, design considerations should extend to operator posture and body positioning and ensure that the door openings and location of the RABS glove ports do not prevent risk of operator contact. Tools should be used in place of an operator entering the RABS when possible. Airflow visualization studies should be performed to confirm adequacy under dynamic conditions. Further precautions and controls are required for open-door interventions (1, 6-8). (See Topic 9.)

            
- The number and location of glove ports should be designed based on the need for and ease of performance of interventions, in particular, in locations where First Air principles can be followed.

            
- Materials and equipment within the RABS should be positioned to avoid crowding and the need to reach over exposed sterile products, materials, and surfaces.

            
- The design and positioning of a RABS filling line should prevent the use of swing conveyors to pass from the front to the back of the filling line.

            
- The RABS design should consider, under risk assessment, a zone of protection using a UDAF unit to cover, at a minimum, the open-door radius. The positions must be determined by a risk analysis and should consider typical open-door activities, such as the setup of stopper bowls or feeding lanes.

            
- The dynamic use of the RABS, where there are inherent and/or corrective interventions being performed and equipment is operating, needs to be confirmed by airflow visualization studies (AVS) to demonstrate that unidirectional flow of air is occurring, and First Air principles are maintained.

            
- The use of automated process steps (e.g., sterilization in place (SIP) after installation of the filling line), and intervention-reducing technology (e.g., rapid transfer port (RTP) filling path or components loading as closures, to install EM samplers for preventing mobile air sampler transfer) should be considered to minimize interventions during setup, operations, and sampling.

            
- The use of robotics and advanced automation should be considered during the design of a new RABS line to increase the level of sterility assurance by removing operator interventions for critical processes (e.g., the setup of the filling path). When using robotics in the aseptic environment for aseptic filling, the design and operating principles must be carefully evaluated for operation suitability within a cleanroom environment. Robotic systems, regardless of type, bring a certain risk to the unidirectional airflow due to a tendency to generate turbulence. Therefore, robots should not be used for the sake of using robotics, but rather should bring a benefit for the aseptic filling process. Computational fluid dynamics (CFD) and airflow visualization studies (static and dynamic) should verify the impact of the robot to the unidirectional airflow and its impact on First Air. Besides the robot itself the requirements to meet first air also applies for any tools the robot is carrying and connections made on the robot (e.g., media hoses etc.). In addition to considerations regarding impact to First Air, cleanability, disinfection and accessibility to the robot also require consideration.

        

        

**Rationale**

        

All interventions into a RABS (i.e., open-door intervention) and within the RABS (i.e., closed-door intervention) in the vicinity of exposed sterile product and critical surfaces can add the risk of microbiological contamination to sterile product. Where possible, the elimination or reduction of these activities through process design, equipment layout, technology, and automation can reduce risk. Where activities cannot be eliminated or reduced, process and equipment design that allows for proper aseptic technique and practices can reduce risk. Where interventions cannot be eliminated or reduced in number, modifying these activities to reduce risk factors can reduce the overall relative risk.

    

    

        

### 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 Key Concepts

            

**介入 (Intervention) 的分類與風險層級：**

            

                
- **Inherent Interventions（固有介入）：**製程設計中預期會發生的操作，如 EM 取樣、零件調整等

                
- **Corrective Interventions（糾正介入）：**因異常情況而需要的操作，如排除卡瓶、調整偏移等

                
- **Open-door Interventions（開門介入）：**需要打開 RABS 門的操作 — **風險最高**

                
- **Closed-door Interventions（關門介入）：**透過手套口完成的操作 — 風險相對較低

            

            

**PDA 的介入管控哲學（優先順序）：**

            

                
1. **消除 (Eliminate)：**透過設計讓介入不需要發生

                
2. **減少 (Reduce)：**降低介入的頻率

                
3. **修改 (Modify)：**改變介入方式以降低風險因素（如用手套口取代開門）

            

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 Key Notes

            

**機器人與自動化 — 不是萬靈丹：**

            

PDA 對機器人採取審慎態度：「robots should not be used for the sake of using robotics, but rather should bring a benefit for the aseptic filling process.」

            

機器人在無菌環境中的關鍵挑戰：

            

                
- 機器人運動會產生紊流 (Turbulence)，破壞 UDAF

                
- 機器人攜帶的工具、軟管連接同樣需要滿足 First Air 要求

                
- 需要透過 CFD（計算流體動力學）和 AVS 驗證其對氣流的影響

                
- 可清洗性、消毒可行性、可及性都是額外的設計挑戰

            

        

        

            

#### 比喻說明 Analogy

            

RABS 的介入管控就像飛機駕駛艙的設計哲學：

            

                
- **消除介入** = 自動駕駛（Autopilot）處理所有例行操作

                
- **減少介入** = 只在關鍵時刻需要機師手動操作

                
- **修改介入** = 即使需要手動操作，也透過操縱桿而非直接觸碰引擎（手套口 vs 開門）

                
- **開門介入** = 機師在飛行中打開引擎艙蓋 — 顯然風險極高，只有在絕對必要時才做

            

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 — UDAF 保護區設計

            

PDA 提出一個重要設計概念：**Zone of Protection（保護區）**— UDAF 氣流覆蓋範圍至少應涵蓋門的開啟半徑。這意味著即使在開門介入時，關鍵區域仍有正壓 UDAF 氣流保護，降低外部低等級空氣侵入的風險。

            

另外，禁止使用 Swing Conveyor（擺動輸送帶）從充填線前方通過後方，因為這會要求操作員跨越暴露的無菌產品上方，違反 First Air 原則。

        

        

            

#### 實務應用 Practical Application

            

**CDMO 新線設計場景：**您正在為一條新的無菌充填線設計 RABS 系統。客戶要求具備「全自動充填路徑建立」能力。

            

                
- **Step 1：**盤點所有介入點 — 列出 Setup、運行中固有介入、可能的糾正介入

                
- **Step 2：**逐一評估 — 哪些可以透過自動化/機器人消除？哪些可以從開門改為手套口操作？

                
- **Step 3：**若導入機器人 — 必須進行 CFD 模擬與 AVS 確認氣流影響

                
- **Step 4：**所有無法消除的介入 — 設計手套口位置、評估 First Air 路徑、制定 SOP

            

            

關鍵：每個決策都要有風險評估支持，並納入 CCS 文件。

        

        

            

#### 練習思考 Practice Questions

            

                
1. PDA 為什麼不建議以「減少介入次數」作為製程變更的出發點？（提示：思考因果關係 vs. 結果）

                
2. 在機器人導入評估中，CFD 模擬與 AVS 各自驗證的重點是什麼？它們是互補還是可以擇一？

                
3. 如果一個糾正性介入需要開門操作，PDA 建議在開門前應確認哪些條件？

                
4. 「Zone of Protection」的 UDAF 覆蓋範圍設計如何影響 RABS 的總體尺寸與成本？

            

        

    

⇧

# Section 1b: Topic 1 RABS Design (Q1.7 - Q1.12)

    

RABS 設計考量（第二部分）：開門介入預防、設置風險、建材維護、高效價化合物、環境監測與改裝設計

    

PDA Points to Consider No. 12 (2025): Restricted Access Barrier Systems | p23 - p33

    

### 本章學習目標

    

        
- 理解如何透過設計審查與程序控制**預防充填期間的開門介入**（Open-Door Interventions），以及不可避免時的風險緩解措施

        
- 掌握設置（Setup）階段降低 Grade A 環境污染風險的**最佳實務做法**，包括由上而下組裝、主/副操作員模式等

        
- 了解 RABS **建材選擇與維護設計**的關鍵要求（316SS、衛生設計、耐化學性）

        
- 認識在 cRABS 中處理**高效價化合物**（Highly Potent Compounds）時的正壓/負壓設計矛盾與解決方案

        
- 掌握**線上環境監測（In-line EM）**設備的工程設計考量，包括粒子計數器、活性空氣採樣器的安裝位置

        
- 理解 RABS **改裝（Retrofitting）**的典型場景、設計要點與 First Air 驗證方法

    

    

### 本節目錄 Table of Contents

    

        Q1.7 預防開門介入
        Q1.8 設置期間風險最小化
        Q1.9 建材與維護設計
        Q1.10 高效價化合物設計
        Q1.11 線上環境監測設計
        Q1.12 改裝與介面設計
    

Q 1.7 How can open-door interventions be prevented during filling?

    

        

### 原文內容 Original Text

        

**Recommendation**

        

RABS are designed with the goal of operating predominately as a closed system. Where open-door interventions may be required, appropriate measures must be taken to mitigate the potential for increased risk to the aseptic process.

        

Detailed design reviews of the production process undertaken at the onset of design can help avoid or minimize the need for open-door activities during the filling operation (1). These reviews should consider, but not be limited to, the following:

        

            
- Since the open-door barrier manual set-up process presents the highest risk of contamination of the Grade A zone when entering sterilized parts, the design of the set-up operation should be assessed using QRM principles to reduce any unnecessary risk.

            
- Following QRM principles, RABS design and operation should avoid the need for open-door interventions so after the last bio-decontamination at set up the barrier doors remain closed until batch end. Primarily inherent and corrective interventions should be via barrier closed and any open-door intervention fully justified and rare.

            
- RTPs used for introduction of pre-sterilized process components, consumables, product containers and closures plus EM plates if required to be changed or recovered for incubation during aseptic manufacturing operations.

            
- Use of robotic systems and automation that drives intervention free processing including introduction of EM systems that do not rely on growth media plate change (e.g., real time continuous viable monitoring).

            
- Design considerations equally extend to consideration of the use and position of glove ports and should be considered in conjunction with the intended operations to define access requirements within the enclosed system and the type of operations for which interventions may be required.

            
- Design considerations extend to the use of clean-in-place (CIP)/SIP and single-use systems for fluid or powder pathways.

        

        

Periodic reviews of the type, frequency, and duration of interventions for the filling process should be reviewed to inform the next periodic aseptic process simulation (APS) protocol and to otherwise inform a potential engineering or other control solution that may be introduced to eliminate the need for future similar open-door interventions (1, 4, 9).

        

Notwithstanding these considerations, not all possible events that may be encountered during manufacturing operations can be considered during the design or early stages of RABS introduction for a new product or process. Rather, the intent of a well-designed aseptic program involving the use of barrier technology is to ensure that the RABS protection concept is the primary focus and continuously assessed, with the aim of eliminating or reducing the need to open the barrier during filling activities. **When a closed-door intervention is possible to address an issue, an open-door intervention must be prohibited.**

        

Procedural controls should be established to ensure that adequate provisions are included in governing procedures and processes for such unavoidable scenarios and should extend to a detailed review and documentation including, but not limited to:

        

            
- Preassessment of airflow visualization studies (AVS) and positive-pressure differentials to ensure that positive airflow from the enclosure to the external environment can be maintained prior to opening doors. A pre-intervention assessment should also extend to a documented review of what needs to be performed and whether the activity can be considered comparable to a preexisting intervention (1, 4, 9).

            
- Consideration of whether the unqualified intervention represents a departure from critical controls established and whether a deviation or formal risk assessment is required in support of finalizing and undertaking the planned intervention. The need for additional EM data, personnel monitoring requirements, sterility sample requirements, particulate-monitoring data and alarm review should be considered. An assessment of whether a media qualification and AVS may be required prior to release of the batch should also be understood and documented.

            
- A robust disinfection of the nonproduct-contact surfaces, implicated by the open-door activity using appropriately qualified disinfectants. If necessary, to ensure there is no disinfectant residue, the use of 70% IPA after disinfection should be considered.

            
- Consideration of need for batch segregation and/or discarding of any filled product or components that may have been compromised or placed at unnecessary risk during the intervention.

            
- Line clearance to eliminate open containers and/or components as applicable that may be in the vicinity of the intervention.

            
- Confirmation that Grade A conditions have been reestablished prior to recommencing filling.

        

        

            "Note: Although not recommended, in rare cases, an unanticipated corrective intervention may be required that necessitates open-door operator intervention (e.g., to mitigate equipment challenges). In such cases, the inherent increased risk to the product requires careful consideration in line with formal QRM principles and should inform future engineering controls or other provisions that may be introduced with the aim of eliminating recurrences or the requirement for the open-door intervention. Before the intervention is executed, it needs to be risk assessed. If the risk-assessment does not support the execution of the intervention, it should not occur."
        

        

**Rationale**

        

By design, the intent of a RABS or other barrier system is to separate the operator from the critical process zone to reduce the overall risk of contamination. Since interventions within a barrier system pose the highest risk to the aseptic core, the aim of any barrier technology, combined with a system of (engineering) controls, should be to reduce or eliminate any unnecessary interventions. Hence, the use of the barrier technology in conjunction with a system of controls comprising suitable design, robust quality systems, and aseptic oversight is required.

    

    

        

### 導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

        

            

#### 核心概念解析 Key Concepts

            

**Open-Door Intervention（開門介入）：**操作員必須打開 RABS 門才能進行的操作。這是 RABS 環境中**風險最高**的事件，因為它直接破壞了屏障系統的核心保護功能 -- 將人與 Grade A 關鍵區域隔離。

            

**Closed-Door Intervention（關門介入）：**透過手套口（Glove Ports）在不打開門的情況下完成的操作。風險顯著低於開門介入，是 RABS 運行期間的首選方式。

            

**核心原則：**當閉門介入可以解決問題時，**必須禁止開門介入**。這不是「建議」，而是一條明確的禁令。

        

        

            

#### 比喻說明 Analogy

            

想像你在進行一場精密的**心臟手術**：手術室的正壓環境就像 RABS 的 UDAF 氣流保護。如果助手每次遞器械都要打開手術室大門，走廊的細菌就會湧入。最好的做法是透過一個**傳遞窗**（就像 RTP 快速傳遞口）把器械送進來，或者讓機器人自動遞送（就像自動化系統），手術室門從頭到尾不需要打開。

            

萬一必須開門（比如緊急搬入大型設備），必須先確認走廊已清潔、正壓仍維持、所有暴露的無菌表面已覆蓋 -- 這就是文件中描述的「程序控制」。

        

        

            

#### 重點提示 Key Notes

            

**EU Annex 1 的嚴格立場：**歐盟法規明確要求充填期間的開門介入應「極為罕見」（very rare）。PDA 本文更進一步指出，在設計階段就應透過 QRM 評估將其消除。這意味著：

            

                
- 開門介入不能作為「標準操作」存在於 SOP 中

                
- 每次開門介入都應觸發偏差調查或正式風險評估

                
- 需要評估是否需要額外的 EM 數據、人員監測、無菌樣品等

                
- 必須確認 Grade A 條件已恢復後才能重新開始充填

            

            

**批次隔離考量：**開門介入後，可能需要將受影響的已充填產品或元件進行隔離或銷毀，這是一個重大的商業損失。因此，在設計階段投資消除開門介入需求，遠比事後處理更具成本效益。

        

        

            

#### 實務應用 Practical Application

            

**場景：**你的 CDMO 工廠正在設計一條新的 RABS 充填線。設計團隊提出需要 12 個手套口，但預算有限。如何決策？

            

                
- **步驟 1：**列出所有預期的固有介入（Inherent Interventions）和可能的矯正介入（Corrective Interventions）

                
- **步驟 2：**對每個介入進行 QRM 評估：能否透過自動化消除？能否透過 RTP 替代？

                
- **步驟 3：**剩餘必須手動完成的介入，確認手套口位置能覆蓋所有需求

                
- **步驟 4：**在 Mock-up 階段驗證每個介入都能在閉門狀態下完成

            

            

投資於 RTP 和自動化的前期成本，可能在第一次避免開門介入引發的偏差調查時就回收了。

        

        

            

#### 練習思考 Practice Questions

            

                
1. 為什麼文件特別強調「當閉門介入可行時，開門介入必須被禁止」？這與一般的「盡可能避免」措辭有何不同？

                
2. 如果你的 RABS 充填線在生產中發生了一次未預期的開門矯正介入，列出你需要執行的所有後續程序控制步驟。

                
3. 文件提到應定期審查介入的類型、頻率和持續時間，並將結果納入下次 APS 方案。這種「介入驅動的 APS 設計」如何提升無菌保證水平？

            

        

    

Q 1.8 How can contamination risks of Grade A environments and compromise of sterilized component sterility be minimized during setup?

    

        

### 原文內容 Original Text

        

**Recommendation**

        

Setup, if done through closed doors via the glove ports, requires fewer precautions; however, setup most often requires activities through open doors. If that is the case, there are several ways to minimize the risk:

        

            
- Operate with only one door open at a time.

            
- As much as possible, equipment should be assembled prior to sterilization to avoid the need for aseptic connections. Sterilized items should be introduced with protective covers or sterile boxes and those covers or boxes should only be removed after the doors have been closed through the glove ports. For legacy systems, where removal of protective covers after the doors are closed is not possible, alternative approaches must be considered and documented as part of the CCS. (See Topic 6.)

            
- Utilize a "top down" approach to line build, when possible, so installation is not occurring over an exposed critical surface (e.g., stopper hopper, stopper slide, stopper bowl).

            
- Don additional gowning, such as sterile sleeves or longer gloves (1).
